> Self-assessment dropped two reader candidates that did not
> survive verification: (a) [HIGH anon] /themes lede `9 in the
> index, 3 featured this month — 12 we'd defend in a group chat`
> flagged as mis-adding — false positive; `ListsHero.tsx:26`
> defines `indexCount = stats.total - stats.featuredCount` so
> the 9 IS by construction the non-featured count, and 9 + 3 =
> 12 is the correct math; the existing `ListsHero.test.tsx`
> pass-28 #295 case (`lede shows the math inline when featured
> + index split`) pins `featuredVal + indexVal === stats.total`;
> (b) [LOW anon] /themes/best-finales #05 entry header `THE
> TRAITORS · S02` does not disambiguate US vs UK — the catalog
> show itself (`content/shows/traitors.md` slug `traitors`)
> renders without `US` in any chrome (catalog name, /shows tile,
> /shows/traitors hero), so introducing the disambiguation on
> the themed-list surface would create a convention the parent
> catalog does not carry; the show's own tagline names "The
> American adaptation" + "Peacock" network tile already anchor
> the identity. Six findings filed (1 HIGH, 2 MED, 3 LOW):
> (i) [HIGH] [anon] cross-surface voice/honesty drift — every
> editorial byline attributes to `tiered.tv Editors` (plural):
> `src/app/shows/[show]/season/[slug]/page.tsx:311 + 379` canon
> entry author + visible byline `Canon entry by tiered.tv
> Editors`, `src/components/featured-themes/FeaturedThemes.tsx:34`
> `Cross-canon · curated by tiered.tv editors`,
> `src/components/canon/ShowRanking.tsx:98` `One ranking, written
> by editors who have rewatched every season at least twice`,
> every theme frontmatter `curator: 'tiered.tv Editors'` default
> in `src/content/schemas.ts:235`. Then `/about` admits the
> opposite twice — `content/legal/about.md:29` `the editor's
> call — one person, one position per season` and line 78 `An
> experiment. Built and operated by one person.` A first-time
> visitor on the natural season → /about or themed-list →
> /about navigation hits the contradiction on a single click.
> Same defect class as pass-26 #282 (`Every voter has watched`
> flat overclaim contradicted by the weighting ladder on /about).
> (ii) [MED] [authed] /themes "By tone" group head label
> (`GROUP_HEAD_LABELS.tone` in `src/lib/themes-format.ts`)
> mis-classifies four of six visible entries —
> `best-reunion-specials` is a format slice, `best-post-merge`
> is a structural region, `best-returnees` is a casting
> structure, `firsts` is a chronological position; only
> `loudest arcs` (best-comeback-seasons) and `rookie casts`
> (best-newbie-casts) are genuinely tonal. The taxonomy label
> promises one kind of cut and delivers another, which makes
> the index hard to scan for a reader trying to use the toggles.
> (iii) [MED] [anon|authed] /themes/best-finales #06 residual
> `artist*` cognate after pass-30 #301 stripped `real artists` —
> entry title (`content/themes/best-finales.md:50`) now reads
> `A final lip-sync that pays off a finale built on real
> artistry.` and body opener (line 51) is `Season 6 spends its
> run building toward a finale of working drag artists, and the
> last episodes deliver — runway moments still replayed, a
> lip-sync stretch with genuine stakes.` Two `artist`-stem words
> inside one entry's six lines reads like the previous fix was
> applied at one node rather than across the entry. (iv) [LOW]
> [anon] /themes/best-finales #01 (Amazing Race S07) doubles
> `live sprint` inside one ~50-word card — title (line 20) `A
> final leg that proves the format's live sprint is built right.`
> + body opener (line 21) `The Race always ends on a live
> sprint, and Season 7 plays that structure at full strength`.
> Pass-28 #297's `closing run` rotation off the cross-entry
> phrase-repetition floor swapped #01's title `closing run` →
> `live sprint` AND body opener `closing run` → `final leg`, so
> the rewrite traded the cross-entry repetition for a
> within-entry one — same defect class, narrower scope.
> (v) [LOW] [anon] /themes/best-finales #05 (Traitors S02)
> lands `table` three times in ~55 words — title (line 44) `The
> Round Table tightening into the final banishment the format
> was built for.` + body (line 45) `the table smaller and
> louder each night. That last seat at the table is where the
> US adaptation proves it can hold the tension all the way
> down.` `Round Table` is the format's named furniture so one
> use is load-bearing, but two more body occurrences land as
> head-noun overuse on the same card. (vi) [LOW] [anon] /about
> voting-mechanics paragraph (`content/legal/about.md:39`) ends
> with `Brigade rate-limits run behind the scenes and should
> never bite a normal reader.` `Brigade` is community-moderation
> jargon (referring to vote-brigading — coordinated upvote /
> downvote campaigns) — every other piece of /about reads in
> plain language (`one vote per reader`, `change your mind
> within 72 hours`, `flagged comments enter a human-reviewed
> mod queue`), so this one cold-jargon noun is the obstacle on
> a sentence the page needs the reader to absorb (it's the
> trust line promising rate-limits won't catch them by
> accident). Spoiler discipline P0 unchanged across all six
> findings (voice / chrome / taxonomy / prose edits only; no
> per-season verdict, winner, elimination, or canon-position
> exposure on any surface).

> sit too close. Spoiler discipline P0 unchanged across all
> four findings (chrome ordering + voice edits only; no per-
> season winner / elimination / finale beat exposed).

- [x] [HIGH] [anon] cross-surface editorial-byline drift: every editorial attribution on the site is plural (`tiered.tv Editors` / `tiered.tv editors` / `editors who have rewatched`) while `/about` admits the opposite twice in plain prose. Concrete observed surfaces: (1) season-page byline — rendered HTML at `/shows/survivor/season/heroes-vs-villains` reads `CANON ENTRY BY TIERED.TV EDITORS` (source: `src/app/shows/[show]/season/[slug]/page.tsx:379` literal `Canon entry by <span className="who">tiered.tv Editors</span>` + matching `author: 'tiered.tv Editors'` JSON-LD at line 311); (2) themed-list curated-by — `content/themes/<slug>.md` `curator` frontmatter defaults to `'tiered.tv Editors'` via `src/content/schemas.ts:235` and renders on every `/themes/[theme]` detail page hero; (3) featured-themes strip on `/` home — `src/components/featured-themes/FeaturedThemes.tsx:34` literal `Cross-canon · curated by tiered.tv editors` (lowercase); (4) show-page canon intro — `src/components/canon/ShowRanking.tsx:98` literal `One ranking, written by editors who have rewatched every season at least twice. We argue with the community out loud — but we ship one number.` (plural verb + plural subject). Then `/about` flatly contradicts the plural framing: `content/legal/about.md:29` reads `The Editor's Canon is the editor's call — one person, one position per season, an 80–120 word reason.` (singular possessive, explicit `one person`) and line 78 reads `An experiment. Built and operated by one person. Free to use.` A first-time reader on the natural season → /about path (or themed-list → /about, or featured-strip → /about) hits the contradiction on a single click — the bylines promise a team, /about admits a solo operation, the reader's trust takes the hit on whichever surface they read second. Bearings voice is `knowledgeable peer — confident, warm, plain-spoken, never pretentious` (`plan/bearings.md:370`); plural-editor framing on every editorial surface and a one-person admission on /about reads as ad-copy plurality undercutting the page that owes the truth, same defect class as pass-26 #282 (`Every voter has watched` flat claim contradicted by the weighting ladder on /about). The `/about` `Become an editor` section (lines 67-74) does anticipate a future plural editorship `New editors come in by invitation after a draft round` — but the current state is one person, and the bylines should match the current state, not the aspirational one. Fix options: (a) **primary path** — singularize the attribution everywhere the rendered chrome reads it. (a2) `src/content/schemas.ts:235` change the `curator` default from `'tiered.tv Editors'` → `'tiered.tv editor'` (the singular form), then propagate to all 12 themed-list frontmatter files via a single sed-style content drain (`content/themes/*.md` `curator: "tiered.tv Editors"` → `curator: "tiered.tv editor"`). (a3) `src/components/featured-themes/FeaturedThemes.tsx:34` swap `curated by tiered.tv editors` → `curated by the tiered.tv editor`. (a4) `src/components/canon/ShowRanking.tsx:98` swap `written by editors who have rewatched every season at least twice. We argue with the community out loud — but we ship one number.` → `written by an editor who has rewatched every season at least twice. The community argues back; this is one number.` (singularizes the subject + verb + first-person plural — `We argue / we ship` becomes the community-vs-editor framing the rest of /about uses). Keep `/about`'s `Built and operated by one person` line as the anchor; keep `Become an editor` as the aspirational pluralization path. (b) alternative — drop the `one person` admission on /about and lean into a small editorial collective (requires a second editor in practice; content cost real, not a one-tick fix). Fix options: (a) **primary path** — unpack the term inline so the trust line lands plainly: `Rate-limits run behind the scenes to catch coordinated voting campaigns, and should never bite a normal reader.` (adds ~9 words, names the function in plain language, removes the cold jargon). Recommended (a) — preserves the trust-line role, removes the cold jargon, single-sentence edit with no new term introduced. - [x] [HIGH] [anon|authed] /shows Amazing Race A-tier tagline outputs broken grammar: `a cross-continent route mechanic that has held its shape across twenty-five of starting lines.` The phrase `twenty-five of starting lines` is ungrammatical — a word is missing between `twenty-five` and `of`. Confirmed source: `content/shows/amazing-race.md:11` `tagline:` reads `... has held its shape across {yearsWord} of starting lines. ...`. The `{yearsWord}` token (defined in `src/lib/show-tenure.ts:129`) substitutes a spelled-out years number ONLY — it does NOT inject the word `years` after itself. Every other corpus use of `{yearsWord}` pairs the token with an explicit `years` word in the literal (see `src/lib/__tests__/show-tenure.test.ts:117,126` — `spent {yearsWord} years rediscovering what it is`). The Amazing Race tagline omits that pairing, so the rendered output is the bare number + `of` + noun — broken grammar on the main catalog surface every visitor sees when browsing shows, and on the longest A-tier blurb on that page. Fix: edit `content/shows/amazing-race.md:11` `tagline:` to insert `years` after `{yearsWord}` — final reads `has held its shape across {yearsWord} years of starting lines.` (matches the canonical `{yearsWord} years` pattern the tenure helper was designed for). Pin: a regression class-check in `scripts/content-check.ts`'s existing `collectYearTenureIssues` invariant — every show frontmatter `tagline` containing the literal `{yearsWord}` must also contain the literal substring `{yearsWord} years` (i.e., the token must be followed by ` years`), with the same `TENURE_ANCHOR_ALLOWLIST` escape hatch if a future tagline needs a different construction (e.g., `{yearsWord}-year run`). The check is cheap, catches the entire class, and lifts at content-author time rather than at production render. Pin 2: add a colocated case to `src/lib/__tests__/show-tenure.test.ts` documenting the contract that `{yearsWord}` substitutes the number only and authors must supply the surrounding noun explicitly — currently the tests show the pattern by example but don't pin the contract. Spoiler discipline P0 intact (tagline-prose-only edit; no per-season verdict). The pin landed as a new sibling helper `collectYearTokenPairingIssues` in `scripts/content-check.ts` (rather than extending `collectYearTenureIssues` literally — the existing helper reads loader-materialized text where the token is already substituted, so it cannot see the raw `{yearsWord}` literal). The new helper reads each show's source markdown directly (via `showFile()` + `gray-matter`) and asserts: any `tagline` or `card_tagline` field containing `{yearsWord}` must also contain `{yearsWord} years`. - [x] [MED] [anon] /shows/survivor mixes two mutually-exclusive mental models of the Community Rank on the same scroll. The site-wide vote question — `Does this belong in the community top 10?` (home `src/components/home/HomeDualCallout.tsx:17-18`, every season's vote block default `src/app/shows/[show]/season/[slug]/page.tsx:318`, /about "How voting works") — is a binary yes/no top-10 ballot. A first-time reader who reads "does it belong in the top 10?" then sees a shift card saying "now #44 of 50" cannot reconcile the two — is the question binary or ordinal? Technically both are accurate descriptions of different planes of the same data (the yes/no question is the prompt the reader responds to; the ordinals are derived from approval-percentage rollups across all "in"/"out" votes), but the page doesn't give the reader a bridge between them. The page jumps from a top-10 question to a #44-of-50 answer with no sentence connecting the two. Source: `src/components/home/HomeDualCallout.tsx:17`, `src/app/shows/[show]/season/[slug]/page.tsx:318` (top-10 framing); `src/components/composition/__tests__/ShiftCard.test.tsx:45,62` ("Slid N spots" / "Climbed N spots" ordinal vocabulary). Recommended (a) — preserves the existing community-data display and resolves the comprehension gap with one editorial sentence. - [x] [MED] [anon] / home `<HomeDualCallout>` Community Rank card closes with `Every voter has watched the season end to end.` (`src/components/home/HomeDualCallout.tsx:18-20`) — stated as a flat fact. But `/about` "How voting works" admits explicitly that there is no watched-it gate at the input layer: `Long-standing accounts carry the most weight. Anonymous-guest votes count at 0.1×. Accounts under 7 days old count at 0.25×.` (`content/legal/about.md:37-38`). Anonymous guests can vote without signing in, without any watched-it attestation, and without any review of their history; the weighting ladder is the only thing keeping their vote from carrying full force. So the home claim "Every voter has watched the season end to end" is not true at the input layer — it is only approximately true at the *weighted* layer (an anonymous guest's "have not watched" vote counts at 0.1×). The home page is the editorial trust surface; stating a falsifiable claim that the /about page immediately disqualifies undercuts the brand promise of plain-spoken honesty. The two reads collide on a single navigation step (home → about) and the contradiction is one a reader will notice before they cast their first vote. Source: `src/components/home/HomeDualCallout.tsx:18-20` ("Every voter has watched the season end to end.") vs `content/legal/about.md:37-38` (the 0.1× / 0.25× / 1.0× weighting ladder). Fix options: (a) **primary path** — soften the home claim to acknowledge the weighting mechanic, e.g. `Signed-in voters self-attest they watched the season end to end; anonymous votes count at 0.1× of a signed-in vote.` (names the mechanic the /about page details, ~150 chars); (b) drop the line entirely and let the weighting be the editorial signal at the surface that explains it (the /about page already carries the mechanic); (c) reframe as an aspirational stance rather than a flat fact, e.g. `We weight votes so the people who watched carry the most weight.`. Recommended (a) — preserves the editorial substance (we trust watched voters), matches the actual mechanic, and reads as plain-spoken rather than overpromised. Pin: extend `src/components/home/__tests__/HomeDualCallout.test.tsx` with a negative regression case asserting the live-pane blurb does NOT match `/Every voter has watched/i` AND a positive case asserting it mentions the weighting mechanic (matches `/(weight|0\.1|signed-in|self-attest|attest)/i`). - [x] [MED] [authed] Mobile chrome at 375px renders the full nav row inline — `tiered.tv / Shows / Lists / About / ⌕ Search / @e2e / Sign out` — with no hamburger collapse and `Sign out` exposed as a top-bar text link on every authed page. The text technically fits within the 375px viewport (scrollWidth === innerWidth, no horizontal scroll, mechanical reflow gate stays clean), but it puts a one-tap-away destructive action immediately beside the user handle on a small touch target, on every page. A user mis-tapping `@e2e` (intending to land on their own profile) and hitting `Sign out` instead is a real and recoverable-but-annoying error class — they re-auth via magic link, which takes a minute and may interrupt a vote or comment in flight. Two reasonable mobile UX fixes: (a) move `Sign out` behind the `@e2e` handle (the handle becomes a tap-to-reveal small menu with `Your record` and `Sign out` as the two items), so the top bar holds nav links only and signing out requires a second deliberate tap; or (b) collapse all secondary chrome behind a hamburger menu at < 480px breakpoint, which is the broader pattern but a bigger styling shift. Recommended: (a) — scoped to the user-island, no broader chrome refactor. The desktop chrome can keep `@e2e / Sign out` inline because the touch target is larger and the visual hierarchy is clearer. Locate: the auth-island component the phase-36 work hydrated (header right-side user controls). - [x] [LOW] [anon] The `/shows/[show]` canon/community tab control (`src/components/canon/CanonTabSwitch.tsx`) renders each tab as `<span class="cp-tab-marker">01</span><span><span class="cp-tab-name">Editor's Canon</span><span class="cp-tab-cap">curated</span></span>` — the name and the state cap are adjacent inline spans with no whitespace or separator between them, and the `<button role="tab">` carries no `aria-label`. On desktop the two read as a single run-together token (`Editor's Canoncurated`, `Communitylive`); on mobile CSS line-breaks the cap so it separates. The button's accessible name therefore computes to `01Editor's Canoncurated` / `02Communitylive`, which a screen reader announces as one mashed token. Evidence: desktop capture text `01 / Editor's CanonCURATED / 02 / CommunityLIVE` vs mobile `01 / Editor's Canon / CURATED`. Fix: give each `<button>` an explicit `aria-label` (e.g. `aria-label="Editor's Canon — the curated ranking"` / `"Community — the live ranking"`) so the accessible name is clean regardless of the visual span packing; the visible run-together is acceptable as a styled lockup but the a11y name should not be. - [x] [MED] [anon] /shows declares a three-tier confidence ladder (S / A / B) in its legend strip — "B tier means we haven't watched everything twice yet — when we have, the show moves up" — but the rendered ladder contains zero shows in B. The page flows S (2 shows) → A (11 shows) → footer, with the B band absent entirely. A first-time visitor reading the legend then scrolling the ladder sees a named tier vanish from the surface that introduced it; the editorial-confidence framing the page is built on reads either as a missing render or as over-promised legend copy. Root cause is content-shape, not page code: every show in `content/shows/<slug>.md` currently carries `tier: S` or `tier: A` — no show is authored at `tier: B`, so the tier-grouping renderer correctly emits an empty band and the page elides it. Fix (two paths): (i) **content path** — promote at least one show to `tier: B` (or demote one from A) so the legend's promise is delivered; the `tier` enum in `CLAUDE.md` is explicitly an editorial confidence statement, and a B-tier show is not a content defect, it's an honest editorial signal; (ii) **page path** — render an explicit empty-band placeholder (`B — nothing here yet.`) when no shows occupy the tier, so the ladder structure honors the legend even when a band is empty; the placeholder reads as honesty about the editorial process the legend describes. The page path is the lower-effort fix; the content path is the truer fix. Recommend page path now + content path as a content-curator backlog item. (URL: /shows, source: critique-pass-14) — 9e2ac61 — issue: #202 — RESOLVED f304756 (page path): `TierSection.tsx` now always renders the `<section>` wrapper + `<TierHead>` (with `count={shows.length}` so the count line reads "0 Shows" honestly) plus a new `.tier-empty` placeholder (`"Nothing here yet."`) in place of `.shows-grid` when the tier holds no shows; the previous `if (shows.length === 0) return null` early-return is gone. The legend in `<HowTiersMove>` now has a B band to refer to on every render. Hero lede + SEO meta description stay honest about the populated subset — the critique-pass-11 #181 invariant holds (they only name tiers that carry shows). New `.tier-empty` styles in `src/styles/shows.css` (italic serif, dashed `--color-line-soft` border, centered, 48px vertical padding desktop / 32px mobile) deliberately read as a deliberate placeholder, not a CSS bug. `TierSection.test.tsx` flips the "renders nothing" case to pin the placeholder render (section wrapper + `data-tier` + count "0" + `.tier-empty[data-empty=true]` body + no `shows-grid`). E2e `shows-index.spec.ts` three updates: (1) `tierOrder` is now always `['S','A','B']`; (2) hero-lede `data-tier-coverage` matches the *populated* subset (sections containing a `shows-grid`), not the rendered subset; (3) B-tier status-pill assertion gates on the section containing a `shows-grid` rather than on the section itself. The content path (promoting a show to tier B) stays a content-curator backlog item — no content change in this fix. - [x] [MED] [anon] / footer `TIERED.TV` column lists four destinations — `About the canon` (`/about`), `How voting works` (`/about#voting`), `Spoilers policy` (`/about#spoilers`), `Become an editor` (`/about#editors`) — but `/about` carries none of the `voting`, `spoilers`, `editors` anchor ids. All four links resolve to the same scroll position on `/about`. A first-time visitor reading the footer sees four distinct destinations and clicks two or three to compare; each click lands at the page top with no visible difference, which reads as broken links or as four labels for one undifferentiated page. This is a navigation-honesty defect — the footer is making promises the destination does not keep. Fix: add `<section id="voting">`, `<section id="spoilers">`, `<section id="editors">` wrappers around the existing `/about` content sections. No copy changes needed — the sections already exist as headed editorial blocks; only the anchor ids are missing. Lowest-effort fix in the queue. - [x] [HIGH] [anon] /shows nine of thirteen show taglines close on the identical "Ranked without <verb> a single <noun>." template — read top-to-bottom on the tier-list page the repeating clause scans as fill-in-the-blank generation, not a knowledgeable peer writing per show. Verified on disk via grep: Drag Race ("Ranked without spoiling a single crowning."), Love Island UK ("...final couple."), GBBO/Bake Off ("...Star Baker."), Project Runway ("...finale collection."), Bachelorette ("...hometown."), Love Island US ("...recoupling."), The Challenge ("...elimination."), Bachelor ("Ranked without giving away a single final rose."), Big Brother ("Ranked without ruining a single eviction."). Top Chef has no such tag; Amazing Race uses a different shape ("We've ranked every leg of every one"); Survivor's tagline is longer-form. The inconsistency makes the repeating nine stand out more, not less. The site-wide "No spoilers" promise is already carried structurally by the chrome (header + footer `<ShieldBadge>` + the home-page brand promise) — every per-show repetition is editorial dead weight. Fix: drop the trailing "Ranked without <verb> a single <noun>." clause from at least six of the nine offenders and let each show's tagline close on its own editorial observation, the way Top Chef and Amazing Race already do. The clause's content is already covered site-wide; the tagline space is editorial real estate that should land an idea unique to that show. Pin with a `scripts/content-check.ts` invariant (lax→strict in the existing `STRICT` / `CROSS_SHOW_STRICT` / `YEAR_TENURE_STRICT` pattern) asserting at most N shows carry the templated trailing clause (initial floor: ≤ 3; final strict floor: ≤ 1) — same shape as the cross-show-coverage and year-tenure invariants already in place. Spoiler discipline P0 unchanged — editorial-voice rewrite only. (URL: /shows, every show home-page card surface that quotes the tagline, source: critique-pass-12) — 60abb0d — issue #187 — RESOLVED at c4f0e6c: content-curator rewrote all ten offenders (the nine the critique named plus Traitors, which uses the same template — "Ranked without naming a single traitor."). Nine had the trailing clause dropped outright; each tagline now closes on the editorial observation already present in the penultimate sentence (Bachelorette → "warmer, sharper, and more willing to let the lead drive."; Bachelor → "running uninterrupted since 2002."; Love Island UK → "summer and winter editions included."; Project Runway → "still the one to beat."; Bake Off → "and somehow the most watchable."; The Challenge → "the genre's true combat league."; Traitors → "faster than anyone expected."; Love Island US → "finally found its footing on Peacock."). Drag Race was rebuilt as a two-sentence tagline matching siblings: "17 seasons of queens at a Los Angeles workroom, sewing through mini-challenges and lip-syncing for their lives on a pink-lit runway. The format that built a global drag economy and still sets the bar every other franchise chases." Big Brother extended the existing closer with a clause ("…and still the loudest room on summer television") rather than ending on the fragmentary "invented the genre.". Pinned with `scripts/content-check.ts` `collectTaglineTemplatedTailIssues()` + new `TAGLINE_TAIL_STRICT = true` toggle — strict floor 0, because the rewrite drained every offender in one tick (skipped the lax intermediate per the critique's "lax→strict in the STRICT / CROSS_SHOW_STRICT / YEAR_TENURE_STRICT pattern" guidance — no daylight to keep). Eight colocated tests in `src/content/__tests__/content-check.test.ts` pin the regex shape across the four verb forms (spoiling / ruining / naming / giving away), the multi-word noun phrases (final couple, Star Baker, finale collection), the legal "Ranked by …" sibling (Top Chef), the legal "We have ranked every single one" sibling (Survivor / Amazing Race), and a live-catalog integration check reading zero offenders against the production content tree. Spoiler discipline P0 intact — editorial-voice rewrite only, zero spoiler reasoning revisited. Verify green: leg1 tokens + typecheck + no-raw-img + unit (incl. 8 new cases) + 127 script tests + content:check (13 shows / 298 seasons / 13 canons / 12 themes / 3 legal docs), leg2 build (374 static pages), leg3 1348 e2e.

- [x] [MED] [anon] /themes eight of ten themed-list blurbs close on the same count-of-shows tail ("across <N> different franchises" / "<N> shows, <M> [thing-noun]") — verified across `content/themes/best-*.md` blurb fields. Best premieres: "across six different franchises." Best finales: "six shows, seven landings." Best newbie casts: "six shows' worth of rookie rosters." Best returnee seasons: "five shows, one premise landed." Best post-merge runs: "Across five franchises." Best firsts/locations/comeback: same construction. The tail duplicates the structural "N SHOWS COVERED" / "N ENTRIES" stat strip that every /themes card AND every /themes/<theme> hero already renders — the blurb is paying twice for the same fact, and the parallel construction across eight of ten blurbs reads as one writer using one template (same class as the /shows tagline tail above). Fix: drop the count-of-shows tail from at least five of the eight offenders and let each blurb close on the editorial observation it actually has (already present in the prior sentences). Pin in the editorial drain via `.claude/agents/content-curator.md` + `skills/ship-content.md` Rule 3 — themed-list blurbs do not restate the show count; the chrome already renders it structurally. Optional lax-mode `content-check` invariant (floor: ≤ 3 blurbs carrying the count-of-shows tail) on the same pattern as the /shows tagline gate above; both can ship as one pure-script helper. Spoiler discipline P0 unchanged. (URL: /themes, every /themes/<theme> card surface that quotes the list blurb, source: critique-pass-12, issue: #191) — 60abb0d — RESOLVED 9dc9418: rewrote ten themed-list `description` fields (best-comeback-seasons, best-finales, best-location-reveals, best-newbie-casts, best-non-winning-runs, best-post-merge, best-premieres, best-returnees, best-villain-editing, firsts) to drop the count construction outright; each blurb now closes on the editorial observation it already carried. best-reunion-specials (named-shows construction) + survivor-pillars (`category: single`, counts seasons) were already clean. Pinned with `collectThemeDescriptionCountTailIssues()` in `scripts/content-check.ts` + new `THEME_COUNT_TAIL_STRICT = true` toggle — strict floor 0, since the rewrite drained every offender in one tick (skipped the lax intermediate per the same lax→strict pattern STRICT / CROSS_SHOW_STRICT / YEAR_TENURE_STRICT / TAGLINE_TAIL_STRICT use; no daylight to keep). Two umbrella patterns covered: (A) `\bacross\s+<N>\s+(?:different\s+)?(?:franchises?|shows?)\b` catches `across six different franchises.`, `Across five franchises,`, `Seasons across six franchises`; (B) `\b<N>\s+shows[,'’]` catches the punch-list `six shows, seven landings.` and the possessive `six shows' worth`. Ten colocated tests in `src/content/__tests__/content-check.test.ts` pin the regex shape across both umbrellas (5 offender shape cases incl. across-different / across-bare / across-shows / punch-list / possessive), the two intentional carve-outs (named-shows + `<N> seasons`), a 4-offender batch case, and a live-catalog integration check reading zero offenders against the production content tree. Brief updates: `.claude/agents/content-curator.md` (new "Description-discipline" sub-rule alongside the existing Title-discipline rule) + `skills/ship-content.md` Rule 3 (new bullet under Cross-canon coverage). Spoiler discipline P0 intact — editorial-voice rewrite only. Verify green: leg1 1948 unit (incl. 10 new cases) + 127 script + content:check (13 shows / 298 seasons / 13 canons / 12 themes / 3 legal docs), leg2 build, leg3 1348 e2e.

- [x] [MED] [anon] /themes all ten themed-list TITLES on disk share one syntactic mold — "<plural noun> that <past-tense verb> <optional object>" (verified via `grep -h "^title:" content/themes/best-*.md`): *Location reveals that announced themselves / Finales that stuck the landing / Premieres that earned it / Comeback seasons that landed / Non-winning runs that defined the season / Post-merge runs that delivered / Newbie casts that arrived ready / Villain edits that ran the season / Returnee seasons that paid off / Reunion specials that closed the loop*. On `/themes` itself the ten titles sit in a category-grouped list and the parallelism is visible top-to-bottom; on the home page's `HomeListsStack` four titles stack adjacent in immediate succession and the syntactic uniformity reads as templated rather than authored. The bearings voice law says plain sentences over clever ones and the design law warns against AI-generated tells; ten-for-ten on one syntactic shape is the canonical example. Fix: re-author three to four titles to break the mold — drop the relative clause for at least two (e.g. *Newbie casts that arrived ready* → *Rookie casts that showed up ready*, *Location reveals that announced themselves* → *Locations that did the talking*) and rewrite one or two into a different shape entirely (a noun-only or imperative title — *The premieres that earned the rest of their seasons* / *Comebacks the franchises actually needed*). Author into `.claude/agents/content-curator.md` Title-discipline block: themed-list titles vary syntactically across the catalog; no more than N of M may share the "X that Y-ed Z" relative-clause shape (initial floor: ≤ 5/10; strict floor: ≤ 4/10). Spoiler discipline P0 unchanged. (URL: /themes, /, every surface that quotes themed-list titles, source: critique-pass-12, issue: #190) — 60abb0d — addressed 361a89b (5/10 retitled to non-clause shapes; Title-discipline block pinned in content-curator brief)

The two intentional departures from the row's literal recommendation: (a) kept the `upvote / downvote` terms because the live VotePair UI still ships up/down arrow buttons (the eac1163 closure for the prior LOW #257 documented the affordance — dropping the terms would re-open that gap); the new copy leads with the question and frames the buttons as the answer, so the post-#240 framing wins without contradicting the live UI; (b) kept the weighting table (Anonymous 0.1× / Accounts under 7 days 0.25× / Accounts 7+ days 1.0×) because it is accurate to the DB (`supabase/migrations/20260513000004_votes.sql:38` + `20260513000005_cast_vote_rpc.sql:107-123`) and /about is the granular surface where granular truth belongs — the home + season pages collapse to "one reader, one vote" for brand simplicity, and /about reframes the math as a secondary mechanic ("long-standing accounts carry the most weight") rather than the headline of how voting works. Pin: `src/app/(default)/about/__tests__/page.test.tsx` expanded the prior 2-case #257 suite (which only pinned upvote/downvote + [+]/[−] regression guards) to an 8-case #258 suite — positive pins for (1) "belong in the community top 10" question framing, (2) "upvote or downvote" mechanic terms, (3) "per reader" scope, (4) "72 hours" change window, (5) "updates weekly" recompute cadence (all with `\s+` whitespace tolerance because the source markdown wraps at 65 cols and the exact phrase may span a line break in `body_md`); negative pins for (6) the prior [+] / [−] glyphs (#257 regression guard preserved), (7) any "per session" scope claim (#258 regression guard), (8) any "flip it whenever" unlimited-flip claim (#258 regression guard). Bidirectional contract: a regression back to the pre-#240 system fails AND dropping the new copy entirely also fails. Spoiler discipline P0 unchanged (copy edit only). Verify green: leg1 tokens + typecheck + no-raw-img + 187 unit files / 2248 tests (incl. expanded /about 10-case suite — 2 import-smoke + 8 copy contract) + 127 script tests + content:check (13 shows / 298 seasons / 13 canons / 12 themes / 3 legal docs), leg2 build (374 pages), leg3 1359 e2e.

- [x] [MED] [authed] scripts/critique-walk.mjs captures page innerText immediately after the `load` event, before client auth islands hydrate — the authed pass-2 walk produced two false-positive HIGH auth-state findings; the walk should settle for network-idle / island hydration before capture (URL: n/a, source: critique-pass-2) — issue #125 — RESOLVED this commit: `walk()` navigated with `page.goto(target, { waitUntil: 'load' })` and captured `document.body.innerText` immediately — before the header auth-state island (`HeaderView`) had run its mount `useEffect`, which fetches `GET /api/auth/me` and only then re-renders the chrome between signed-out and signed-in. So the authed walk read the pre-hydration SSR DOM ("Sign in"), filing false-positive HIGH auth-state findings (two withdrawn in pass 2; a third authed observation — the season comment composer reading "Sign in to comment" against a `@e2e / Sign out` header — withdrawn in pass 3 precisely because it was indistinguishable from this artifact). Fix: two new exported helpers + a per-page settle. Before navigation the walk arms `page.waitForResponse` for the `/api/auth/me` request (pre-`.catch()`'d so a timeout can't surface as an unhandled rejection while `goto` is still in flight); after the `load`-event `goto` it calls `settleForHydration`, which awaits that response (pinning the one request whose result changes the chrome) then `page.waitForLoadState('networkidle', { timeout: SETTLE_TIMEOUT })` so the island re-render — and any other island, e.g. the season comment composer — has flushed. Both waits are best-effort: a `networkidle` timeout and an auth-fetch rejection are both swallowed, so a slow page or a chatty third-party beacon delays the capture, never fails it. New `SETTLE_TIMEOUT` (8000ms, exported, `--settle-timeout` override) bounds the worst case under the 20s nav timeout. New pure export `isAuthMeRequest(url)` — pathname-exact `/api/auth/me` match, origin/query agnostic, no throw on a non-URL — is the `waitForResponse` predicate. §5a: 7 new colocated tests in `scripts/__tests__/critique-walk.test.mjs` — `SETTLE_TIMEOUT` shape, `isAuthMeRequest` (matches with/without query + cross-origin, rejects sibling endpoints + sub-paths, non-URL → false no throw), `settleForHydration` (awaits auth then networkidle in that order, swallows a networkidle timeout, swallows an auth-response rejection and still runs the idle wait, handles the pre-caught null shape). No new URL or page family — a change to the critique tooling, not the product — so no e2e fixture row. Verify green: leg1 tokens + typecheck + no-raw-img + unit + 99 script tests + content:check (13 shows/298 seasons/13 canons/12 themes/3 legal docs), leg2 build, leg3 1319 e2e.

Applied once in `loadProfile` (`src/app/(default)/u/[handle]/page.tsx`) where `ProfileActivity → ProfileView` is shaped, so it covers both the visible byline and the JSON-LD in a single chokepoint, and protects rows already polluted in the DB as well as future ones. No schema or migration — the `email` column is unchanged; this fixes only the public *render*.
